{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-12-11 16:00:45","updatedTime":"2020-12-11 16:00:45","title":"How to Take Sharp Images","link":"https://digital-photography-school.com/blog/?p=169","description":"<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-take-sharp-digital-images/\">How to Take Sharp Images</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. It was authored by <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/author/darren/\">Darren Rowse</a>.</p>\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1200\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=1200%2C1200&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"taking sharp images ibis\" class=\"wp-image-199346\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=300%2C300&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=150%2C150&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=717%2C717&#38;ssl=1 717w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-55.jpg?resize=50%2C50&#38;ssl=1 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Taking sharp images is something that most photographers want &#8211; but clean, crisp, sharp images can be difficult to achieve.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Before we start exploring how to improve sharpness, let&#8217;s talk about the main causes of a lack of sharpness:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>Poor focus</strong> &#8211; The most obvious way to get images that are &#8216;un-sharp&#8217; is by shooting them out of focus. This might be a result of focusing on the wrong part of the image, being too close to your subject for the camera to focus, selecting an aperture that produces a very narrow depth of field, or taking an image too quickly without checking that it is in focus.</li><li><strong>Subject movement </strong>&#8211; Another type of blur in shots is the result of your subject moving; this is generally related to the shutter speed being too slow.</li><li><strong>Camera shake</strong> &#8211; You can get blur if you, as the photographer, generate movement while taking the image. This often relates to shutter speed and/or the stillness of your camera.</li><li><strong>Noise</strong> &#8211; <a aria-label=\"Noisy shots (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-avoid-and-reduce-noise-in-your-images/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Noisy shots</a> are pixelated and look like they have lots of little dots over them (get up close to your TV, and you&#8217;ll get the same effect).</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"ways-to-take-sharper-images-tips-for-beginners\">10 Ways to Take Sharper Images: Tips for Beginners</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s a list of 10 basic things to think about when shooting &#8211; so you can get consistently sharp images.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Note: There&#8217;s also <a aria-label=\"a lot you can do in Photoshop (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/take-control-sharpening-in-photoshop/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">a lot you can do in Photoshop</a> <em>after </em>taking your images!)</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"976\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=1500%2C976&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"how to take sharp images dahlia\" class=\"wp-image-199333\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=300%2C195&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=600%2C390&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=768%2C500&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-12.jpg?resize=717%2C467&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p><script type=\"text/javascript\" src=\"https://500px.com/embed.js\"></script></p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"hold-your-camera-well\">1. Hold your camera well</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>A lot of blur in the photos that I see is a direct result of camera shake (i.e., the movement of your camera for that split second when your shutter is open). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>While the best way to tackle camera shake is to use a tripod (see below!), there are many times when using one is impractical, and you&#8217;ll need to shoot while holding your camera. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;ve written a tutorial previously on <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-hold-a-digital-camera/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">how to hold a digital camera</a>, but in brief:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Use both hands, keep the camera close to your body, and support yourself with a wall, tree, or some other solid object.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"use-a-tripod\">2. Use a tripod</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Regular readers of this site will have seen our articles on <a aria-label=\"tripods (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/tripod-buying-guide/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">tripods</a> and know that we&#8217;re a big fan of using tripods as a way to reduce (and even eliminate) camera shake. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>While tripods are not always practical, the result you&#8217;ll get when you do go to the effort of hauling one around can be well worth it.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><b>Related</b> <strong>Article</strong>: <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/a-beginners-guide-to-tripods/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">A Beginner&#8217;s Guide to Tripods</a></p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"select-a-fast-shutter-speed\">3. Select a fast shutter speed</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Perhaps one of the first things to think about in your quest for sharp images is the <a aria-label=\"shutter speed (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/shutter-speed/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">shutter speed</a> that you select.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, the faster your shutter speed, the less impact camera shake will have, and the more you&#8217;ll freeze movement in your shots. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>As a result, you reduce the likelihood of two of the main types of blur in one go (<em>subject movement</em> and <em>camera movement</em>). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>But how do you pick the right shutter speed? I recommend the <a aria-label=\"&#34;rule&#34; for handholding (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/back-to-basics-what-is-the-reciprocal-rule-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">&#8220;rule&#8221; for handholding</a>:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><i>Choose a shutter speed with a denominator that is larger than the focal length of the lens. </i></p>\n\n\n\n<p>So:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>If you have a lens that is 50mm in length, don&#8217;t shoot any slower than 1/60th of a second</li><li>If you have a lens with a 100mm focal length, shoot at 1/125th of a second or faster</li><li>If you are shooting with a 200mm lens, shoot at 1/250th of a second or faster</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>Keep in mind that the faster your shutter speed is, the larger you&#8217;ll need to make your aperture to compensate (see the next section!). And this will mean you have a smaller depth of field, which makes focusing more of a challenge.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"choose-a-narrower-aperture\">4. Choose a narrower aperture</h3>\n\n\n\n<p><a aria-label=\"Aperture (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/aperture/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Aperture</a> impacts the <a aria-label=\"depth of field (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/understanding-depth-field-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">depth of field</a> (the zone that is in focus) of your images. Decreasing your aperture size (which means increasing the f-number) will increase the depth of field &#8211; meaning that the zone in focus will include both close and distant objects.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Do the opposite (by moving to f/4, for example), and the foreground and background of your images will be more out of focus. Therefore, you&#8217;ll need to be exact with your lens focusing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Keep in mind that the smaller your aperture, the longer your shutter speed will need to be &#8211; which makes moving subjects more difficult to keep sharp.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"keep-your-iso-as-low-as-possible\">5. Keep your ISO as low as possible</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The third element of the exposure triangle is <a aria-label=\"ISO (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/iso-settings/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\"><em>ISO</em></a>, which has a direct impact on the noisiness of your shots. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Choose a larger ISO, and you&#8217;ll be able to use a faster shutter speed and a smaller aperture (which, as we&#8217;ve seen, helps with sharpness). On the other hand, this will increase the noise in your shots. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Depending on your camera (and how much you plan to enlarge your images), you can probably get away with using an ISO of up to 400 (or even 800 or 1600 on some cameras) without too much noise. But for pin sharp images, keep the ISO as low as possible.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"if-you-have-image-stabilization-use-it\">6. If you have image stabilization, use it</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Many cameras and lenses are now being released with different forms of image stabilization (IS). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Image stabilization won&#8217;t eliminate camera shake, but can definitely help reduce its impact. I find that using IS lenses gives me an extra two or three stops (i.e., I can drop the shutter speed by around two to three stops) when handholding my camera. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Keep in mind that IS helps with camera movement but not subject movement &#8211; so it&#8217;s not helpful in low-light action scenarios. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Also, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/image-stabilization-on-tripods/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" class=\"ek-link\">don&#8217;t use image stabilization when you mount your camera to a tripod</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"nail-focus-as-often-as-possible\">7. Nail focus as often as possible</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Perhaps the most obvious technique to work on when aiming for sharp images is focusing. Most of us use our camera&#8217;s autofocusing, and this works well &#8211; but don&#8217;t assume that your camera will always get it right.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Make sure you check what part of the image is in focus before hitting the shutter. And if the focusing isn&#8217;t right, then try again or switch to <a aria-label=\"manual focus (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/dont-afraid-manual-focus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">manual focus</a>. This is particularly important if you&#8217;re shooting with a large aperture (small depth of field), where even the slightest focusing error can result in your subject being noticeably out of focus.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"taking sharp photos ibis\" class=\"wp-image-199334\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-11.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Most modern cameras have a range of focus modes you can shoot in, and choosing the right focusing mode is very important. <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/choosing-a-focus-mode/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">You can learn how to do that <strong>here</strong></a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"make-sure-your-lenses-are-sharp\">8. Make sure your lenses are sharp</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>This one is for DSLR and mirrorless owners:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have the budget for it, invest in good-quality lenses, because this can have a major impact upon the sharpness of your images.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For example, shortly after buying my first DSLR, I was in the market for an everyday zoom lens that would give me the ability to have both wide and telephoto zoom capabilities. I bought a <a aria-label=\"Canon EF 28-135mm lens (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Canon28-135\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 28-135mm lens</a>. It was a good lens (and reasonably priced), but it wasn&#8217;t as sharp as some of my other lenses.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>A few months later, I borrowed a <a aria-label=\"Canon EF 24-105mm &#34;L&#34; lens (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Canon24-105\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Canon EF 24-105mm &#8220;L&#8221; lens</a> (&#8220;L&#8221; is Canon&#8217;s professional series of lenses) from a friend, and I was amazed by the difference in sharpness between the lenses. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>While the first lens was good for what I paid for it, I ended up going for an upgrade. The new lens is now almost permanently attached to my camera.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"get-your-eyes-checked\">9. Get your eyes checked</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Since I was young, I&#8217;ve worn glasses. But in recent years, I&#8217;ve been a little slack in getting my eyes checked. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Recently, I got them tested for the first time in a number of years, and I was surprised to find that they&#8217;d deteriorated significantly. Getting new glasses improved a number of areas of my life, one of which was my photography. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Also connected to this is checking the <em>diopter</em> on your camera, if it has one. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>What&#8217;s a diopter? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s usually a little wheel positioned next to your viewfinder that lets you tweak the sharpness of the image you see when shooting. The diopter is particularly useful for people with poor eyesight, because you can use it to compensate for your vision (so you won&#8217;t have to remember to wear glasses when out shooting!).</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"clean-your-equipment\">10. Clean your equipment</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Recently, my wife and I went on a window-cleaning frenzy at our place. Over the previous months, the grime on our windows had gradually built up without us really noticing it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>But when we did clean the windows, we were amazed at how much more light got through and how much better the view outside was!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The same can be true for your lens. <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/clean-care-camera-gear/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Keep it clean (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Keep it clean</a>, and you&#8217;ll eliminate the smudges, dust, and grime that can impact your shots. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Similarly, a clean image sensor is a wonderful thing if you have a DSLR or a mirrorless camera, as getting dust on it can produce noticeable blotches in your final images.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/take-sharp-images-10.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"taking sharp photos little blue heron\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"use-your-lenss-aperture-sweet-spot\">11. Use your lens&#8217;s aperture sweet spot</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Lenses have some spots in their aperture ranges that are especially sharp. In many cases, the ultimate &#8220;sweet spot&#8221; is one or two stops from the maximum aperture. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>So instead of shooting with your lens wide open (i.e., where the f-numbers are smallest), pull it back a stop or two, and you might get a little more clarity in your shots. <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/find-your-lens-sweet-spot/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Learn more about identifying your lens&#8217;s sweet spot <strong>here</strong></a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"further-reading-about-how-to-take-sharp-images\">Further reading about how to take sharp images</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Learn more about how to take sharp images with the following tutorials:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/advanced-tips-for-tack-sharp-images/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new They let you apply rich, detailed edits to your photos that go well beyond what you can accomplish in other programs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, adjustment layers can be a bit difficult to understand if you&#8217;re used to a more streamlined application like <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/lightroom-what-is-it-and-when-should-you-consider-it/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Lightroom</a>, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/apple-photos-an-under-appreciated-post-processing-software-powerhouse/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Apple Photos</a>, or <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/luminar-4-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Luminar</a>. But with a bit of practice, you can easily master Photoshop adjustment layers and take your photo editing to the next level!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-magnolia.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers magnolia seed\" class=\"wp-image-198225\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-magnolia.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/nikon-d7100-review/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon D7100</a> | <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/writers-favorite-lens-50mm-f1-8/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">50mm f/1.8G</a> | 50mm | 1/500s | f/2.8 | ISO 250</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"what-are-photoshop-adjustment-layers\">What are Photoshop adjustment layers?</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>When you open a picture in Photoshop, you can&#8217;t just start dragging sliders to change its appearance. Before you can do much of anything, you need to start with <a aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/photoshop-layers-for-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">layers</a>, which serve as the bedrock of everything that makes Photoshop so powerful.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers leaf\" class=\"wp-image-198226\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://geni.us/dPSNikonD7100\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Nikon D7100 (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon D7100</a> | <a href=\"https://geni.us/Nikon50mmf1-8\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">50mm f/1.8G</a> | 50mm | 1/250s | f/2.8 | ISO 450</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>To help visualize the concept of adjustment layers, think about a physical picture sitting on your desk. If you wanted to give the picture a green tint, you could simply drape a sheet of green cellophane over it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>That&#8217;s <em>exactly </em>how adjustment layers work in Photoshop: They let you change the visual properties of your image without destroying the underlying file. You can add as many adjustment layers as you want and use them to change things like <a aria-label=\"white balance (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/introduction-to-white-balance/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">white balance</a>, <a aria-label=\"exposure (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/learning-exposure-in-digital-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">exposure</a>, <a aria-label=\"hue/saturation (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-use-the-hue-saturation-adjustment-in-photoshop-a-video-tutorial/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">hue/saturation</a>, and over a dozen other properties.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In other words: </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Photoshop adjustment layers are like stacking sheets of digital cellophane on top of your images. Each layer can be controlled individually and combined with <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/layer-masks-in-photoshop-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">layer masks</a> to apply edits to specific parts of your images. All of this might seem needlessly complicated compared to the simplicity of other programs, but once you get the hang of Photoshop adjustment layers, you&#8217;ll never want to go back.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers dandelion\" class=\"wp-image-198301\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-dandelion.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Nikon D7100 | 50mm f/1.8G | 50mm | 1/2000s | f/2.8 | ISO 100</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Another way to think about Photoshop adjustment layers is by comparing them to panels in the <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/steps-for-getting-started-in-the-lightroom-develop-module/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Develop module of Lightroom (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Develop module of Lightroom</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>However, the Develop panels only offer a handful of adjustments that you can use. Photoshop lets you stack as many layers as you need &#8211; even multiple layers of the same type of adjustment &#8211; so you can tweak your images as much as you could possibly want. There is a bit of a learning curve, but the results are well worth the effort.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"how-to-add-an-adjustment-layer\">How to add an adjustment layer</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The first step when working with adjustment layers is to load an image into Photoshop. Then click on the Adjustments panel, which is usually located above the Layers panel. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>(If you don&#8217;t see the Adjustments panel, go to the Window menu and choose <em>Adjustments</em>.)</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"866\" height=\"808\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?resize=866%2C808&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers\" class=\"wp-image-198302\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?w=866&#38;ssl=1 866w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?resize=300%2C280&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?resize=600%2C560&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?resize=768%2C717&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel.png?resize=717%2C669&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 866px) 100vw, 866px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Load an image into Photoshop and then click the Adjustments panel.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>The Adjustment panel offers sixteen adjustments to choose from, and sorting through all of these can be overwhelming (especially if you&#8217;re used to the simple, straightforward editing parameters available in Lightroom).</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"366\" height=\"256\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel-icons-2.png?resize=366%2C256&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustments\" class=\"wp-image-198456\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel-icons-2.png?w=366&#38;ssl=1 366w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-panel-icons-2.png?resize=300%2C210&#38;ssl=1 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 366px) 100vw, 366px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Each one of these icons is a specific type of adjustment. Hover your cursor over each one to see a brief description.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Some of these adjustments are similar to what you might find in Lightroom, such as <em>Brightness/Contrast</em> and <em>Color Balance</em>. But using the adjustments is much different from working in Lightroom and, in some ways, more complicated. Fortunately, that also means you can get much better results.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To see how this process works, I&#8217;ve included an image (below) that clearly needs some editing. Thankfully, Photoshop adjustment layers are here to help!</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers Minnesota\" class=\"wp-image-198306\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-0.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption><a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/nikon-shooter-fuji-x100f-second-camera/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Fujifilm X100F</a> | 23mm | 1/4000s | f/8 | ISO 200</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;ll start by adding a <em>Brightness/Contrast</em> adjustment layer, which is a simple matter of just clicking the <em>Brightness/Contrast</em> icon in the Adjustments panel. Immediately, two sliders appear, which you can use to make the picture brighter or darker and to add or remove contrast.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"372\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?resize=876%2C372&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Brightness/Contrast editing parameters\" class=\"wp-image-198307\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?resize=300%2C127&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?resize=600%2C255&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?resize=768%2C326&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-sliders.png?resize=717%2C304&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>After clicking an adjustment layer icon, the available editing parameters show up for you to start working with.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>A few seconds later, my picture is much improved, thanks to a brightness boost. However, there is still a lot of work left to do.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers Minnesota\" class=\"wp-image-198313\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-1.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Brightness +75, Contrast -5</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>One other thing happens when you click an adjustment layer icon that you might not notice but is critically important:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Layers panel will create a layer specifically for that adjustment.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"374\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?resize=876%2C374&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"adjustment layers\" class=\"wp-image-198308\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?resize=300%2C128&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?resize=600%2C256&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?resize=768%2C328&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-brightness-contrast-layer.png?resize=717%2C306&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Clicking an adjustment icon automatically adds a new layer to your image with the selected adjustment as its title.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This new layer, along with all the icons associated with it, is what gives an adjustment so much flexibility. In Lightroom, you can enable and disable individual panels in the Develop module, but you don&#8217;t have this level of control over your adjustments.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-default\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"874\" height=\"366\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips.gif?resize=874%2C366&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"masking icon\" class=\"wp-image-198310\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"/></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Note the different icons in the short screen capture above:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul id=\"block-b1f4ab17-015b-4643-9769-acadbb5e0b6b\"><li><strong>Indicates layer visibility</strong>: Click this to hide or show the adjustment.</li><li><strong>Layer thumbnail</strong>: Double-click this to show the editing parameters (sliders, eyedroppers, etc.) for the adjustment layer.</li><li><strong>Indicates layer mask is linked to layer</strong>: Click this to unlink the adjustment layer mask from the adjustment. If you&#8217;re new to adjustment layers, you can just ignore this altogether.</li><li><strong>Layer mask thumbnail</strong>: This is a very tiny preview of the layer mask that is created by default when you click on a new adjustment layer icon. Click this to show the editing parameters of the mask.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>While my picture of the Minnesota sign is better than when I started, it still needs a lot of improvement. The next thing I want to do is set the white balance, but this option is missing from the Adjustments panel. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead, you have to use the <a aria-label=\"Curves adjustment (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/understand-curves-tool-photoshop/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Curves adjustment</a>, then click the gray point eyedropper. Next, click a neutral or slightly gray portion of your image to counteract any color casts. Note that this process essentially replicates the White Balance function of Lightroom.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"938\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?resize=876%2C938&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"curves adjustment\" class=\"wp-image-198314\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?resize=280%2C300&#38;ssl=1 280w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?resize=560%2C600&#38;ssl=1 560w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?resize=768%2C822&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-tooltips-gray-point.png?resize=717%2C768&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Select the gray point tool, then click a slightly gray or neutral area of your photo to set the white balance of the image.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>One thing you might notice is that the Curves options in Photoshop are much more comprehensive than the Curves options in Lightroom. This should give you an indication of how much more flexibility you have with adjustment layers. You can use Curves to do everything you would do in Lightroom, along with much, much more.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The final operation to fix this image involves a Hue/Saturation adjustment layer. Click on the <em>Hue/Saturation</em> icon to bring up a panel that looks like this:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"636\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?resize=876%2C636&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers\" class=\"wp-image-198445\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?resize=300%2C218&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?resize=600%2C436&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?resize=768%2C558&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-hue-saturation.png?resize=717%2C521&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>The Hue/Saturation adjustment layer parameters</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>The key to this panel is the hand icon in the top-left. Click it, then click on a part of your image that you would like to saturate or de-saturate. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>In this case, I want to start with the grass below the sign. Clicking and dragging to the right makes it much greener, and gives a sense of vibrance that is sorely missing from the original.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers Minnesota\" class=\"wp-image-198446\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-2.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>The grass and foreground elements really pop, thanks to a quick tweak with the Hue/Saturation adjustment layer.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This is a good start, but I need to fix the sky, and that is where a layer-based approach really starts to come in handy. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead of editing the sky with the adjustment layer I just created, I can add a new adjustment layer and use <em>that </em>for the sky. This allows me to control my Hue/Saturation edits for individual parts of the image, instead of having just one Hue/Saturation adjustment layer that affects the entire scene.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Minnesota statue with boosted sky colors\" class=\"wp-image-198447\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-3.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>The sky colors are now improved. These edits are applied using a layer separate from the grass edits, and thus can be controlled independently.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>While the resulting picture is much better than the original, there is still some tweaking that needs to be done for it to truly feel finished.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"adjustment-layer-masks-explained\">Adjustment layer masks, explained</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Eagle-eyed observers might notice something amiss with the picture above: </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Minnesota sign now has a purple tint to it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Never fear, adjustment layers are here! Click the white rectangle next to a layer name to edit its mask:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-default\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"560\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=876%2C560&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"layer masks\" class=\"wp-image-198448\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=300%2C192&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=600%2C384&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=768%2C491&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask.png?resize=717%2C458&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>You see, by painting black onto a layer&#8217;s mask, you prevent that area of the photo from being affected by the adjustment. So if you don&#8217;t want the sign to be affected by the Hue/Saturation adjustment layer, simply paint black over the portion of the mask that covers the sign!</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s how it works:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>First, select the <a aria-label=\"Brush tool (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-things-to-know-about-photoshop-brushes/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Brush tool</a> (press <em>B</em> or click the <em>Brush</em> icon in the left-hand toolbar). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Make sure your foreground color is white and your background color is black (to do this quickly, just hit <em>D</em>).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now it&#8217;s time to actually paint the mask. Press the <em>X</em> key to switch between white (revealing) and black (hiding), and the [ and ] keys to increase or decrease the size of the brush. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For tricky shapes like the sign, you can use the Magic Wand tool to select the shape. Then, with the shape still selected, use the Brush tool to mask (remove) the adjustment from that portion of the image.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-default\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers Minnesota\" class=\"wp-image-198449\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-minnesota-4.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>A closer inspection of the Layers panel now shows a black silhouette over the portion that has been masked out of the top Hue/Saturation adjustment layer. I have also renamed the top two layers so as to accurately describe the type of effect they have on the image. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Double-click a layer name to rename it, and press <em>Enter</em> when you finish typing.)</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"560\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=876%2C560&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers\" class=\"wp-image-198450\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=300%2C192&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=600%2C384&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=768%2C491&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-mask-edited.png?resize=717%2C458&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>The mask for the Hue/Saturation Sky adjustment layer shows a black patch where the adjustment has been concealed.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"nondestructive-editing\">Nondestructive editing</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>One mistake some beginners make when editing images in Photoshop is applying adjustments directly to the original photo. This can be done using the <em>Image>Adjustments</em> menu, which gives you common editing options such as <em>Brightness/Contrast</em>, <em>Hue/Saturation</em>, and more. Unlike adjustment layers, these edits are not easy to work with, nor are they easy to alter once they have been implemented.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Photoshop adjustment layers, on the other hand, are nondestructive. You can tweak and change layers <em>after </em>they have been implemented, and you can easily delete them. That&#8217;s why layer adjustments are much more flexible than edits applied directly to an image.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"876\" height=\"560\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=876%2C560&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Photoshop adjustment layers\" class=\"wp-image-198451\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=300%2C192&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=600%2C384&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=768%2C491&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-options.png?resize=717%2C458&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 876px) 100vw, 876px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Adjustment layers can be renamed, re-sorted, locked, disabled, and made transparent. And that&#8217;s just the beginning!</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>You can perform all manner of custom tweaks and changes to adjustment layers, such as:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Showing/hiding a layer by clicking the <em>eye </em>icon</li><li>Editing the adjustment by clicking the <em>light/dark circle</em> icon</li><li>Adjusting the opacity of a layer</li><li>Changing the <a aria-label=\"blend mode (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/first-3-photoshop-blend-modes-need-understand/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">blend mode</a>, which adjusts how the layer interacts with layers below it</li><li>Adjusting the order of the layers by clicking and dragging</li><li>Locking a layer to prevent further changes by clicking the <em>lock </em>icon</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>Photoshop adjustment layers open up new editing possibilities that simply cannot be achieved in Lightroom. For example, the image of a leaf from the beginning of this article can be altered with a selective color adjustment in a matter of seconds. All I need to do is add a Black &#38; White adjustment layer. I can then select the leaf with the Magic Wand tool and paint over the selection on the layer mask.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"leaf in color with black and white background\" class=\"wp-image-198227\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/photoshop-adjustment-layers-leaf-bw.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Adding a selective color black and white effect took about four seconds.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"photoshop-adjustment-layers-conclusion\">Photoshop adjustment layers: conclusion</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you have a <a aria-label=\"Creative Cloud Photography subscription (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://clk.tradedoubler.com/click?p(264300)a(3193397)g(22913526)url(https://www.adobe.com/creativecloud/photography/compare-plans.html?promoid=9DJJ4N49&#38;mv=other)\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Creative Cloud Photography subscription</a>, you can use Photoshop in addition to Lightroom at no extra charge. Now, if the sheer level of options and buttons in Photoshop makes you want to run to the comfort and safety of Lightroom, I get it. I have been there, too, and I still have that feeling from time to time.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>However, learning to use Photoshop adjustment layers is one of the first steps in understanding how powerful and flexible Photoshop can be. If you have not yet tried working with layers, take a moment to test them out. See what layers can do for you. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You might be surprised at how easy it is!</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/photoshop-adjustment-layers/\">Your Quick Guide to Understanding Photoshop Adjustment Layers</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>.
