https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-31.jpg?resize=300%2C126&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-31.jpg?resize=600%2C253&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-31.jpg?resize=768%2C324&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-31.jpg?resize=717%2C302&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Alternatively, you can click around the wheel to select different colors:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"500\" height=\"329\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-32.jpg?resize=500%2C329&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"clicking on the wheel\" class=\"wp-image-200269\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-32.jpg?w=500&#38;ssl=1 500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-32.jpg?resize=300%2C197&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-32.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-32.jpg?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 500px) 100vw, 500px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>And you can further fine-tune the saturation with the left-hand slider:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"512\" height=\"325\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-34.jpg?resize=512%2C325&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"using the saturation slider\" class=\"wp-image-200270\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-34.jpg?w=512&#38;ssl=1 512w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-34.jpg?resize=300%2C190&#38;ssl=1 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 512px) 100vw, 512px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus you can change the brightness of the shadows with the right-hand slider:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"491\" height=\"312\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-45.jpg?resize=491%2C312&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"using the brightness slider\" class=\"wp-image-200271\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-45.jpg?w=491&#38;ssl=1 491w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-45.jpg?resize=300%2C191&#38;ssl=1 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 491px) 100vw, 491px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Personally, my favorite way to select colors is to use the wheel, but start by pushing the Saturation slider all the way up:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"505\" height=\"323\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-36.jpg?resize=505%2C323&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"saturation pushed all the way to its maximum\" class=\"wp-image-200273\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-36.jpg?w=505&#38;ssl=1 505w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-36.jpg?resize=300%2C192&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-36.jpg?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 505px) 100vw, 505px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>That way, you can clearly see the effects of your color grade &#8211; and once you&#8217;ve chosen the right color, you can dial it back. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Also, while it&#8217;s always a good idea to experiment, the best shadow colors are generally <em>cool</em> &#8211; blues, greens, and purples. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;d also recommend paying careful attention to the colors already present in your shadows &#8211; by matching the shadow color with already-existing colors, you can unify the darker parts of your photo and make it even stronger.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>For this flower photo, I like blue-green shadows:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"762\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?resize=1500%2C762&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"blue-green shadows example\" class=\"wp-image-200274\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?resize=300%2C152&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?resize=600%2C305&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?resize=768%2C390&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-37.jpg?resize=717%2C364&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"step-adjust-the-highlights\">Step 2: Adjust the highlights</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Selecting a color for the Highlights wheel is just like selecting a color for the Shadows wheel. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can use the eyedropper tool:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"504\" height=\"1020\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-38.jpg?resize=504%2C1020&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"the highlights eyedropper\" class=\"wp-image-200275\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-38.jpg?w=504&#38;ssl=1 504w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-38.jpg?resize=148%2C300&#38;ssl=1 148w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-38.jpg?resize=296%2C600&#38;ssl=1 296w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 504px) 100vw, 504px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Or you can click on the wheel directly.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, you can also fine-tune with the Saturation slider and the Brightness slider:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"502\" height=\"331\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-39.jpg?resize=502%2C331&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"the brightness slider\" class=\"wp-image-200276\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-39.jpg?w=502&#38;ssl=1 502w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-39.jpg?resize=300%2C198&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-39.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-39.jpg?resize=115%2C75&#38;ssl=1 115w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 502px) 100vw, 502px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Generally, you&#8217;ll want a warmer color for the highlights: an orange, yellow, or red. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>It&#8217;s also a good idea to pay attention to your existing highlight colors. For instance, if your photo has a lot of warm sunlight, such as in the shot of the Black-eyed Susan flowers, you might want to accentuate the yellows with some nice golden highlights:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"775\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?resize=1500%2C775&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"warmer highlights example\" class=\"wp-image-200277\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?resize=300%2C155&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?resize=600%2C310&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?resize=768%2C397&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-40.jpg?resize=717%2C370&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>I&#8217;d also recommend looking at your shadow colors even when adjusting the Highlights wheel. For a nice result, you might choose a color that contrasts with the shadows to create a complementary color pair (as I discussed in the Color Wheel section, above). </p>\n\n\n\n<h3 data-section id=\"step-adjust-the-midtones\">Step 3: Adjust the midtones</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Adjusting the midtones is a bit less common than adjusting the highlights and the shadows. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>For one, if you adjust the midtones, your photo will often take on a more obvious tinted look, because we humans expect midtones to be more neutral compared to colder shadows and warmer highlights. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus, the midtones can correspond to skin tones, which you (generally) want to keep as natural as possible.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So I recommend you be careful when experimenting with the Midtones color wheel. If you do decide you want to make changes, I&#8217;d recommend keeping things closely aligned with the highlights, because too many colors in your scene will start to look messy. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Make sense? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>As you&#8217;d expect, adjusting the midtones is just like adjusting the highlights and shadows. You have the Midtone color wheel that you can click on:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"509\" height=\"1021\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-41.jpg?resize=509%2C1021&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"midtones color wheel\" class=\"wp-image-200278\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-41.jpg?w=509&#38;ssl=1 509w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-41.jpg?resize=150%2C300&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-41.jpg?resize=299%2C600&#38;ssl=1 299w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 509px) 100vw, 509px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Plus your eyedropper:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"502\" height=\"1020\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-42.jpg?resize=502%2C1020&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"midtones eyedropper\" class=\"wp-image-200279\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-42.jpg?w=502&#38;ssl=1 502w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-42.jpg?resize=148%2C300&#38;ssl=1 148w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photo-studio-ultimate-tone-wheels-color-wheel-42.jpg?resize=295%2C600&#38;ssl=1 295w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 502px) 100vw, 502px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Which you can use to give your midtones a slight color grade!</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"acdsees-color-and-tone-wheels-the-next-steps\">ACDSee&#8217;s Color and Tone Wheels: the next steps</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Now that you&#8217;ve finished this article, you know how to make pro-level color adjustments. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And with Photo Studio Ultimate 2021&#8217;s Color Wheel and Tone Wheels tools, you have everything you need to take your color editing to the next level. Photography</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. It was authored by <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/author/hillarygrigonis/\">Hillary Grigonis</a>.</p>\n\n<p>Don&#8217;t let the &#8220;land&#8221; in <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/11-surefire-tips-for-improving-your-landscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"landscape photography (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">landscape photography</a> fool you; a great landscape photo relies just as much on the sky as the land. Boring gray skies make for boring landscape photos, after all! </p>\n\n\n\n<p>That said, capturing a dramatic sky in-camera is trickier than it seems. When the sky is lighter than the land, your camera will typically <a aria-label=\"overexpose (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/learning-exposure-in-digital-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">overexpose</a> it, turning a brilliant blue into a vague and unexciting gray or white.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But with a little fine-tuning, it is possible to capture a sky that is the cherry on top of a great scene! Here are six tips for capturing more dramatic skies in your landscape photography.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"913\" height=\"1500\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?resize=913%2C1500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"dramatic sky cityscape\" class=\"wp-image-198543\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?w=913&#38;ssl=1 913w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?resize=183%2C300&#38;ssl=1 183w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?resize=365%2C600&#38;ssl=1 365w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?resize=768%2C1262&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-1.jpg?resize=717%2C1178&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 913px) 100vw, 913px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"time-it-right\">1. Time it right</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Landscape photography may not require the split-second timing that&#8217;s necessary for capturing a toddler&#8217;s smile or a wide receiver&#8217;s catch, but timing is still a big part of the picture. The sky that&#8217;s gray one day could be bright blue the next. So when planning out a landscape photo, consider how the timing will impact the sky.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Watch for <a aria-label=\"weather patterns (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/time-for-landscape-weather-and-landscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">weather patterns</a> that add interest to a shot, like a storm brewing just above the horizon. Weather plays a big role in the overall mood of the image &#8211; so if you&#8217;re hoping to capture a dark and gloomy shot, head out when the sky is stormy. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>On the other hand, if you&#8217;re hoping to capture a more relaxed or happy photo, look for blue skies dotted with clouds.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1004\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=1500%2C1004&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"blue sky with fluffy clouds\" class=\"wp-image-198544\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=600%2C402&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=768%2C514&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=436%2C293&#38;ssl=1 436w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-2.jpg?resize=717%2C480&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>The time of day matters, too. While the middle of the day will produce the most shadows on the land, it&#8217;s when the sky tends to be the clearest blue. And <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/new-photographers-guide-to-blue-hour/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"just after sunset and just before sunrise (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">just after sunset and just before sunrise</a> is often a good time to capture wispy clouds and a warmer tint of light. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-photograph-a-sunrise/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"sunrise (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">sunrise</a> and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-shoot-landscapes-at-sunset/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"sunset (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">sunset</a> is great for dramatic skies, as well.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"try-the-wrong-white-balance\">2. Try the wrong white balance</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Photography rules are sometimes meant to be broken, including rules about always using the correct <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/introduction-to-white-balance/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"white balance (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">white balance</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You see, the wrong white balance setting can create a more dramatic sky. This is especially true when shooting toward the beginning or end of the day &#8211; using a different white balance preset will adjust the color in the sky.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Auto, Cloudy, and Shade white balance presets will get you an orangish sunset with a light blue sky (with slight variations in warmth depending on the setting you choose). A florescent setting, on the other hand, will typically turn an orange sunset purple with a brilliant blue sky. Tungsten offers a similar effect, but with even deeper colors.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalancepresets.jpg?ssl=1\" alt=\"white balance examples\" title=\"whitebalancepresets.jpg\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"/></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Using Kelvin temperatures to adjust your white balance results in even greater control over the colors in the sky. At around 5500K, you&#8217;ll usually capture a sunny sky with an accurate white balance &#8211; that is, where things that are white are still white in the picture, and where things that are gray are still gray in the picture. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>A higher temperature &#8211; 6500K, for example &#8211; will give the land an orange glow but also enhance the colors in a sunset. A cooler temperature, on the other hand (e.g., 3000K), will play up the blues and purples. By using the Kelvin scale, you have more options for picking a white balance setting that best captures the colors in your photos.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image size-post-large-image wp-image-94784 is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"750\" height=\"500\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?resize=750%2C500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Warm white balance for a warm sky\" class=\"wp-image-94784\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?w=750&#38;ssl=1 750w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/whitebalance160000K.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 750px) 100vw, 750px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Here, the white balance was altered in post-processing to warm up the sky.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>While it&#8217;s always best to get the shot right in-camera, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/raw-vs-jpeg/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"shooting in RAW (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">shooting in RAW</a> offers you even more flexibility when it comes to adjusting the colors in the sky (and the rest of the image, for that matter). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you overdid things by making the shot too warm or too cool, you can easily adjust a RAW photo in post-processing, so that you use the color temperature that best fits the image. If you have a landscape photo that you already shot in RAW, open it and try different white balance presets, or the temperature slider, to see first-hand how shooting with a different white balance would have impacted the shot.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"compose-for-the-sky\">3. Compose for the sky</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>When the sky is more dramatic than the land, why not use that to determine your <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-elements-of-composition-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"composition (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">composition</a>? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Pay attention to where you place the horizon when you are composing your shot. Use the <a aria-label=\"rule of thirds (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/rule-of-thirds/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">rule of thirds</a> to imagine the image is divided into threes, then place the horizon on one of those horizontal lines. If you are shooting a photo with an average-looking sky, try placing the horizon on the upper third of the image, so more of the land is included in the photo, like this:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1199\" height=\"1500\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?resize=1199%2C1500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"horizon high up with a boring sky\" class=\"wp-image-198546\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?w=1199&#38;ssl=1 1199w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?resize=240%2C300&#38;ssl=1 240w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?resize=480%2C600&#38;ssl=1 480w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?resize=768%2C961&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-4.jpg?resize=717%2C897&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>As the sky here isn&#8217;t very dramatic, the higher placement of the horizon improves the composition.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>But if the sky is really dramatic, take advantage of that and include more of it in the frame &#8211; by placing the horizon on the lower third:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"horizon low in the frame with a dramatic sky\" class=\"wp-image-198545\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-3.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>The sky here is dramatic, so the image was composed to show less ground and more sky.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"use-a-filter\">4. Use a filter</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>There are two <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/beginners-guide-buying-filters/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"filters (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">filters</a> every landscape photographer should have in their camera bag in order to capture more dramatic skies. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>The first is a <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/using-graduated-neutral-density-filters-for-landscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"graduated neutral density filter (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">graduated neutral density filter</a>. Now, a regular <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/neutral-density-filters-landscape-photos/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"neutral density filter (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">neutral density filter</a> is like putting sunglasses over your lens &#8211; it limits the light coming in for bright scenes or long exposures. But a <em>graduated </em>neutral density filter places that darkening effect only on a portion of the image. And by positioning the dark portion of the filter over a bright sky, you can properly expose the entire scene. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Without a graduated neutral density filter, the sky will often be overexposed and bland, or the land will be underexposed and dark. With the filter, you can achieve an exposure that works for both portions of the scene. The only downside is that graduated neutral density filters don&#8217;t work as well with an uneven horizon, like when shooting a <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/10-tips-better-cityscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"cityscape (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">cityscape</a>. Graduated neutral density filters come in both circular and square formats, but the square is often preferred because you can place the horizon anywhere in the frame.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The second filter landscape photographers should use to capture more dramatic skies is a <a aria-label=\"polarizing filter (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-use-and-buy-polarizing-filters/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">polarizing filter</a>. Polarizing filters work by adjusting the reflected light coming through your camera lens. Since the sky is blue because of this reflected light, turning the front of the polarizing filter will adjust the intensity of the blues in the sky. Since polarizing filters only affect reflected light, they can still be used when mountains or buildings make the horizon uneven. Polarizing filters are also great for enhancing or removing reflections on water or other shiny surfaces.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1500\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?resize=1000%2C1500&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"polarizing filter example\" class=\"wp-image-198547\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?w=1000&#38;ssl=1 1000w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?resize=200%2C300&#38;ssl=1 200w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?resize=400%2C600&#38;ssl=1 400w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?resize=768%2C1152&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-5.jpg?resize=717%2C1076&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"experiment-with-motion-blur-and-long-exposures\">5. Experiment with motion blur and long exposures</h2>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/step-by-step-guide-to-long-exposure-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Long exposures (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Long exposures</a> aren&#8217;t just for photographing waterfalls. If you use a long enough <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/shutter-speed/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"shutter speed (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">shutter speed</a>, the clouds will blur, too, creating a sky of wispy streaks and a slight feeling of motion. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>To capture <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-capture-motion-blur-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"motion blur (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">motion blur</a> in the clouds, you&#8217;ll need to use a long shutter speed. The best settings will depend a bit on the weather and how much motion blur you&#8217;d like, but you can try starting with a two-minute exposure and adjust up or down from there.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"motion in the sky\" class=\"wp-image-198548\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-6.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>If you are shooting during the day, you may not be able to balance out a two-minute exposure with a narrow-enough <a aria-label=\"aperture (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/aperture/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">aperture</a> or a low-enough <a aria-label=\"ISO (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/iso-settings/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">ISO</a>; instead, you&#8217;ll end up with a photo that&#8217;s way too bright. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>So how do photographers capture motion blur in the clouds when the photo obviously wasn&#8217;t taken at dusk or dawn? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>They use a <em>neutral density filter</em> &#8211; which helps block out some of the light so that you can set a long exposure during the day.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Note that a neutral density filter is the same thing as a graduated neutral density filter, but the entire filter is dark instead of just half of the filter).</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1000\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=1500%2C1000&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"motion in the water and sky due to a long exposure blur\" class=\"wp-image-198549\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=768%2C512&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/tips-for-dramatic-skies-7.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"use-the-adobe-camera-raw-graduated-filter-tool\">6. Use the Adobe Camera RAW Graduated Filter tool</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>While it&#8217;s always best to get the shot right in-camera, there are a few editing tools that can improve the sky in your landscape photos. One of those tools is the <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/improve-your-images-with-the-lightroom-graduated-filter-tool/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Graduated Filter (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Graduated Filter</a> inside <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/quick-beginners-guide-processing-raw-files-photoshop-adobe-camera-raw/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Adobe Camera RAW (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Adobe Camera RAW</a> (this works the same in <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-easy-photoshop-tips-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Photoshop (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Photoshop</a> and <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/brief-introduction-lightroom/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"Lightroom (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Lightroom</a>). </p>\n\n\n\n<p>With the Graduated Filter, you can drag an effect over the sky in your photo. Like an actual graduated filter, the effect will only cover the top portion of the image and gradually fade away, making it possible to create natural-looking edits.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The Graduated Filter tool can be used to adjust the exposure, creating an effect much like an actual graduated neutral density filter. But the tool can also adjust contrast, saturation, clarity, sharpness, and color. That opens up a lot of possibilities for applying edits just to the sky for more drama &#8211; creating effects that sometimes can&#8217;t be done in-camera.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image size-post-large-image wp-image-94789 is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"750\" height=\"498\" id=\"capturing-dramatic-skies-in-your-landscape-photos-conclusion\">Capturing dramatic skies in your landscape photos: conclusion</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The sky can make or break a landscape photo. From timing and composition to filters and post-processing, when you consider the sky as you shoot, you&#8217;ll end up with more dramatic, frame-worthy shots.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Do you have any other tips for creating dramatic skies in your landscape photography? Share them in the comments!</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/6-tips-for-capturing-dramatic-skies-in-your-landscape-photography/\">6 Tips for Capturing Dramatic Skies in your Landscape Photography</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. 16:00:45","updatedTime":"2020-12-11 16:00:45","title":"Focus, Compose, and Expose with Intent in Photography","link":"https://digital-photography-school.com/?p=195459","description":"<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/photograph-with-intent/\">Focus, Compose, and Expose with Intent in Photography</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>. It was authored by <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/author/kevin-landwer-johan/\">Kevin Landwer-Johan</a>.</p>\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1200\" height=\"1200\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=1200%2C1200&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"photograph with intent\" class=\"wp-image-200160\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?w=1200&#38;ssl=1 1200w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=300%2C300&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=600%2C600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=150%2C150&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=768%2C768&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=717%2C717&#38;ssl=1 717w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/12/photograph-with-intent-20002.jpg?resize=50%2C50&#38;ssl=1 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Why do you take photographs? Whatâ€™s your intention each time you press the shutter button? Do you visualize how you want your photo to look before you take it? When you photograph with intent, the pictures you make resonate more with the people who view them.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>All of us have a unique worldview. No two people perceive what they see precisely the same way. Learning to express what you see through the lens of your camera requires paying attention to more than what you are looking at. You must also have <em>intent </em>as to how you want your photos to turn out.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL26746.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Woman on a red couch outdoors for photographing with intent\" class=\"wp-image-196135\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL26746.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. <a aria-label=\"Nikon D800 (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/nikon-d800e-review/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon D800</a> | <a aria-label=\"35mm f/1.4 (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/dps-writers-favorite-lens-why-love-35mm-f1-4/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon 35mm f/1.4</a> | 1/125 sec | f/1.8 | ISO 100 | <a aria-label=\"Manual Mode (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/shoot-manual-mode-cheat-sheet-beginners/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">Manual Mode</a> | Pattern Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"your-camera-does-not-take-photos\">Your camera does not take photos</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Just as a musicianâ€™s instrument or a painter&#8217;s brush creates nothing on its own, your camera does not take photographs. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Instead, the interaction you have with your camera is what creates photos. The quality and creativity of your photographs depends on the level of synergy between photographer and camera. The connection between you and your chosen subject is also significant.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Modern digital cameras are all designed to be as simple as possible to use &#8211; especially consumer-level cameras. Scene modes, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/benefits-shooting-auto-mode/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"auto-exposure (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">auto-exposure</a>, <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/focus-on-autofocus/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"autofocus (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">autofocus</a>, auto-<em>everything</em> allows unskilled photographers to take snapshots that turn out pretty well.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When I was a kid, our neighbors had a pianola. This was a piano that had a handy mechanism: we could push pedals with our feet and the pianola would play tunes. There were special rolls of paper with holes punched in them that could be loaded into the front of the pianola. As we pedaled, the paper roll would turn. The configuration of the holes determined what tune was played. We were playing music without being musicians.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This is similar to using a camera with its auto-functions turned on. It can be fun, and there will be a certain, but limited, satisfaction as pictures are created. Just as we lovedÂ &#8220;playing&#8221; the pianola, you can take photos with minimal creative input or skill.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To take truly wonderful photos, however, you must interact with your camera and your subject with intent. Relying on camera technology to make it easy to take photos will not make you a great photographer.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"woman taking photo\" class=\"wp-image-196136\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL30331.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. <a aria-label=\"Nikon D800 (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/NikonD800\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon D800</a> | <a aria-label=\"35mm f/1.4 (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Nikon35mmf1-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon 35mm f/1.4</a> | 1/400 sec | f/2 | ISO 100 | Manual Mode | Spot Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"know-your-camera-well\">Know your camera well</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Being familiar with your camera and its controls means you can concentrate more on the art of photography. You&#8217;ll no longer be distracted by the technical aspects of the camera.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Learn to control your <a aria-label=\"exposure (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/learning-exposure-in-digital-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">exposure</a>, focus, <a aria-label=\"white balance (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/introduction-to-white-balance/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">white balance</a>, and all the other <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/essential-camera-settings/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"settings (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">settings</a>. As you do this, you will grow in confidence and begin to &#8220;see&#8221; what you are photographing in different ways.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Cameras used in auto-exposure mode tend to make very generically-exposed images. Your camera is programmed to do things in certain ways to produce photos with an even exposure. But the more you take charge of what your camera is doing, the more creative your photography becomes.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Lahu man smoking a bong photograph with intent\" class=\"wp-image-196140\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL50720.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. Nikon D800 | <a aria-label=\"105mm f/2.8 (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://geni.us/Nikon105mmf2-8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener nofollow\" class=\"ek-link\">Nikon 105mm f/2.8</a> | 1/200 sec | f/5.6 | ISO 400 | Manual Mode | Spot Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Understand the <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/metering-modes-and-how-your-camera-meter-works/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"exposure meter (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">exposure meter</a>. Use your <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/fine-tune-your-exposures-with-spot-metering/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"spot meter (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">spot meter</a> to measure the light from different zones in your composition. Experiment with manual exposure settings. Donâ€™t always adhere to what the meter tells you is &#8220;correct.&#8221; Control where you are focusing and the amount of the image that is sharp.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This may all seem a bit overwhelming if youâ€™re new to photography, or if you&#8217;ve been using your camera for years without adjusting the controls. But remember: We could not add any creative expression to the tunes we played with the pianola. Unless you intentionally set your camera&#8217;s controls, your photos will lack creativity.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Monk photographing with intent outdoors at a parade\" class=\"wp-image-196137\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL43681.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. Nikon D800 | Nikon 105mm f/2.8 | 1/200 sec | f/2.8 | ISO 400 | Manual Mode | Spot Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"visualize-your-photographs\">Visualize your photographs</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Think about how you want your photos to look before you take them. Do you want to record a scene exactly as you see it? Or will your frame it in such a way as to exclude some ugly elements?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Make constant choices about what <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/4-things-you-should-know-about-focal-length-and-composition/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"focal length lens (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">focal length lens</a> youâ€™ll use. How much of what you see will you include in the final shot? The same scene photographed with a <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/canon-ef-s-24mm-f2-8-pancake-lens-review/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\"24mm lens (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">24mm lens</a> will look very different than if you back up and photograph it with a 200mm lens.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>How do you want your exposure to look? Will exposing for the highlights or shadows create a more interesting atmosphere? Are there things in the shadow areas you want to hide or reveal? When you have control over your exposure, you have the capability to express yourself in more creative ways.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"Woman standing in a field with a cow\" class=\"wp-image-196141\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i0.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL24666.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. Nikon D800 | Nikon 105mm f/2.8 | 1/2000 sec | f/3.2 | ISO 200 | Manual Mode| Pattern Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Your choice of when you press the shutter release to take the photo can have an important creative influence on the outcome. This is sometimes a matter of a split second, or it can be a matter of waiting for the season to change. Picking the decisive moment when <a aria-label=\"photographing a child playing (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/how-to-go-beyond-the-regular-composition-advice-for-getting-the-best-shots-of-your-kids/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">photographing a child playing</a> versus <a aria-label=\"photographing a landscape (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/11-surefire-tips-for-improving-your-landscape-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">photographing a landscape</a> is very different. But timing is equally relevant to making good pictures.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Are you seeing in <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/understanding-the-basics-of-color/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">color</a> or in <a href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/stunning-black-and-white-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">black and white</a>? Will your subject look more interesting as a monotone image? Will this alter the feeling of the photo? If you are intentional about color as youâ€™re taking photos, youâ€™ll create more compelling images.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"portrait of a novice monk, high contrast black and white \" class=\"wp-image-196138\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?w=1500&#38;ssl=1 1500w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=300%2C200&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=600%2C400&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=768%2C513&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=90%2C60&#38;ssl=1 90w, https://i2.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/KL52156-Edit.jpg?resize=717%2C478&#38;ssl=1 717w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1000px) 100vw, 1000px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Â© Kevin Landwer-Johan. Nikon D800 | Manual Mode | Spot Metering</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<h2 data-section id=\"connect-with-your-subject\">Connect with your subject</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>As you&#8217;re taking photos, think about why you want to photograph your chosen subject. What has drawn you to want to make a picture of this person, thing, or scene? </p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you think about the <em>why</em>, you can start to see your subject in new ways. Being aware of what motivates you can have an influence on how you photograph something.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Does your subject mean something personal to you? How can you show this in the photos you take? There are many ways you can choose to control your camera, or where you take your photos from, that will influence the final shot. Being aware of how you <a aria-label=\"compose (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/5-elements-of-composition-in-photography/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">compose</a> and expose your subjects will help <a aria-label=\"build a story (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/8-tips-storytelling-images/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" class=\"ek-link\">build a story</a> into your images. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Your photos will move from being <a aria-label=\"snapshots  (opens in a new tab)\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/beyond-snapshots-how-to-take-that-fancy-dslr-camera-off-auto-and-photograph-your-life-like-a-pro/\" target=\"_blank\" class=\"ek-link\"><em>snapshots</em> </a>to <em>works of art</em> that have depth and convey meaning.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image is-style-with-caption\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\"><img loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1500\" height=\"1001\" src=\"https://i1.wp.com/digital-photography-school.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/Kayaw-Woman-Portrait-Thailand-KevinLJ.jpg?resize=1500%2C1001&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"black and white portrait of a woman photograph with intent\" class=\"wp-image-196139\" It may seem somewhat abstract when you first try. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>But, like anything creative, the more you apply yourself and practice, the better you will become &#8211; and this will show in your photos.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com/photograph-with-intent/\">Focus, Compose, and Expose with Intent in Photography</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://digital-photography-school.com\">Digital Photography School</a>.
